25:T3e1d,<entryFree id="n36063" key="قَلَبَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">قَلَبَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, A, Mgh, O, Msb, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">قَلِبَ</orth>
                  </form>, (Msb, K.) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">قَلْبٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He altered,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">changed, its,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">his, mode,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">manner, of being;</hi> (A, Mgh, Msb, * K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-1" target="قلّبهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36063"/></foreign> signifies the same, (K,) or is like <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَهُ</foreign> in the sense expl. above and in other senses but denotes intensiveness and muchness; (Msb;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-2" target="اقلبهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> also signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَهُ</foreign> in the sense expl. above, (K,) on the authority of Lh, but is of weak authority. (TA.) Hence, (Mgh,) <hi rend="ital">He inverted it; turned it upside-down; turned it so as to make its upper most part its undermost;</hi> (S, * A, * Mgh, Msb;) namely, a thing; (S;) for instance, a [garment of the kind called] <foreign lang="ar">رِدَآء</foreign>: (A, * Mgh:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-3" target="قلّبهُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36063"/></foreign> has a similar meaning, but [properly] denotes intensiveness and muchness. (Msb. See two exs. of the latter verb voce <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَةٌ</foreign>.) And, (A, K,) like   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-4" target="قلّبهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36063"/></foreign>, [except that the latter properly denotes intensiveness and muchness,] (K,) it signifies <foreign lang="ar">حَوَّلَهُ ظَهْرًا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لِبَطْنٍ</foreign> (A, K) [<hi rend="ital">He turned it over,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">upsidedown</hi> as meaning <hi rend="ital">so that the upper side became the under side;</hi> lit. <hi rend="ital">back for belly;</hi> accord. to the TA, meaning <hi rend="ital">back upon belly</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">ظَهْرًا عَلَى بَطْنٍ</foreign>); but this is hardly conceivable; whereas the former explanation is obviously right in another case: (see 5:) and another meaning of <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَهُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-5" target="قُلبهُ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">he turned it inside-out,</hi> is indicated in the TA by its being added, <hi rend="ital">so that he knew what was in it</hi>].          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  See an ex. voce <foreign lang="ar">قَلَابِ</foreign>. One says, <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ كَلَامًا</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">He altered,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">changed, the order of the words of a sentence</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, by inversion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by any transposition</hi>]. (TA.) [And in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ كَلِمَةً</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He altered,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">changed, the order of the letters of a word, by inversion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by any transposition.</hi>] Es-Sakháwee says, in the Expos. of the Mufassal, that when they transpose [the letters of a word], they do not assign to the [transformed] derivative an inf. n., lest it should be confounded with the original, using only the inf. n. of the original that it may be an evidence of the originality [of the application of the latter to denote the signification common to both]: thus they say <foreign lang="ar">يَئِسَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">يَأْسٌ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">أَيِسَ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-6" target="مَقْلُوبٌ" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n36088"/>مِنْهُ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">formed by transposition,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">metathesis, from it</hi>], and has no inf. n.: when the two inf. ns. exist, the grammarians decide that each of the two verbs is [to be regarded as] an original, and that neither is <foreign lang="ar">مقلوب</foreign> from the other, as in the case of <foreign lang="ar">جَذَبَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">جَبَذَ</foreign>: but the lexicologists [in general] assert that all such are [of the class termed] <foreign lang="ar">مقلوب</foreign>. (Mz, close of the 33rd <foreign lang="ar">نوع</foreign>.) [And <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ</foreign> likewise signifies <hi rend="ital">He changed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">converted,</hi> a letter <hi rend="ital">into</hi> another letter; the verb in this sense being doubly trans.: for ex., one says, <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ الوَاوَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَآءً</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He changed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">converted, the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">into</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And [hence] one says, <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَهُ عَنْ وَجْهِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He turned him</hi> [<hi rend="ital">from his manner, way,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">course,</hi> of acting, or proceeding, &amp;c.]: and Lh has mentioned   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-7" target="اقلبهُ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [in the same sense], but as being disapproved. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ الصِّبْيَانَ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (the teacher) <hi rend="ital">turned away</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">dismissed</hi>] the boys to their dwellings: (Th, A, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">sent them</hi> [<hi rend="ital">away</hi>], <hi rend="ital">and returned them, to their abodes:</hi> and Lh has mentioned   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-8" target="اقلبهم" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> as a dial. var. of weak authority, saying that the former verb is that which is used by the Arabs in this and other [similar] cases. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبْتُ القَوْمَ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">I turned away</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">dismissed</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party;</hi> (Th, S, O;) like as you say <foreign lang="ar">صَرَفْتُ الصِّبْيَانَ</foreign>. (Th, S.) And <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ ٱللّٰهُ فُلَانًا إِلَيْهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">God translated such a one unto Himself, by death:</hi> meaning <hi rend="ital">God took his soul</hi>]; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-9" target="اقلبه" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (K, TA;) whence the saying of Anooshirwán, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-10" target="أَقْلَبَكُمُ" n="10" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ٱللّٰهُ مُقْلَبَ أَوْلِيَائِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">May God translate you with the translating of his favourites</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">مقلب</foreign> being here an inf. n.), meaning, as He translates his favourites]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ عَيْنَهُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">حِمْلَاقَهُ</foreign>, (TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">حِمْلَاقَ عَيْنِهِ</foreign>, (A,) [<hi rend="ital">He turned about,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rolled, his eye,</hi> and therefore <hi rend="ital">the parts of his eye that are occasionally covered by the eyelids,</hi>] on the occasion of anger, (A, TA,) and of threatening. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">قَلِبَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">قَلْبٌ</foreign>; and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36063-11" target="اقلب" n="11" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> likewise, but this is of weak authority, mentioned by Lh; signify also <hi rend="ital">He turned over</hi> bread, and the like, when the upper part thereof was thoroughly baked, in order that the under side might become so. (TA.) And you say, <foreign lang="ar">قَلَبْتُ الإِنَآءَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I turned over the vessel upon its head</hi>]. (Msb, in explanation of <foreign lang="ar">كَبَبْتُ الإِنَآءَ</foreign>.)                      <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">قَلْبٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">heart;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">فُؤَادٌ</foreign>: (Lh, T, S, M, O, Msb, K, &amp;c.:) or [accord. to some] it has a more special signification than the latter word: (O, K:) [for] some say that <foreign lang="ar">فؤاد</foreign> signifies the “ appendages of the <foreign lang="ar">مَرِىْء</foreign> [or œsophagus], consisting of the liver and lungs and <foreign lang="ar">قَلْب</foreign> [or heart]: ” (K in art. <foreign lang="ar">فأد</foreign>:) [and, agreeably with this assertion,] it is said that the <foreign lang="ar">قلب</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">a lump of flesh, pertaining to the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فؤاد</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">suspended to the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نِيَاط</foreign> [q. v.]: Az says, I have observed that some of the Arabs call the whole flesh of the <foreign lang="ar">قلب</foreign>, its fat, and its <foreign lang="ar">حِجَاب</foreign> [or septum?], <foreign lang="ar">قَلْب</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فُؤَاد</foreign>; and I have not observed them to distinguish between the two [words]; but I do not deny that the [word] <foreign lang="ar">قلب</foreign> may be [applied by some to] the <hi rend="ital">black clot of blood in its interior:</hi> MF mentions that <foreign lang="ar">فؤاد</foreign> is said to signify the “ receptacle, ” or “ covering, ” of the heart, (<foreign lang="ar">وِعَآءُ القَلْبِ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">غِشَاؤُهُ</foreign>, [i. e. the pericardium,]) or, accord. to some, its “ interior: ” the <foreign lang="ar">قَلْب</foreign> is said to be so called from its <foreign lang="ar">تَقَلُّب</foreign>: [see 5:] the word is of the masc. gender: and the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">قُلُوبٌ</foreign>.
